# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` — use `repo:^github.com/prometheus/prometheus$` filter
- `github.com/sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common` — use `repo:^github.com/sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common$` filter
- `github.com/prometheus/alertmanager` — use `repo:^github.com/prometheus/alertmanager$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/prometheus/prometheus`, `github.com/sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common`, `github.com/prometheus/alertmanager`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`

# Prometheus PromQL Query Parsing and Validation Pipeline

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that implement the PromQL query parsing and validation pipeline. Identify: the Parser interface and parser struct with ParseExpr and checkAST (in promql/parser/), the Lexer tokenizer, the AST node type definitions (Expr, VectorSelector, BinaryExpr, etc.), the generated yacc parser, the Function registry defining valid PromQL functions, the value type system used for expression type validation, and the Engine that integrates the parser.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: prometheus/prometheus.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `prometheus/prometheus` (prometheus/prometheus)
- `sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common` (prometheus/client_golang)
- `prometheus/alertmanager` (prometheus/alertmanager)
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)

## Summary

I found **14 essential Go source files** across the promql package that implement the complete parsing and validation pipeline:

**Core Parser Components:**
- `promql/parser/parse.go` - Parser interface and implementation with ParseExpr() and checkAST() methods
- `promql/parser/ast.go` - AST node definitions (Expr, VectorSelector, BinaryExpr, AggregateExpr, Call, etc.)
- `promql/parser/lex.go` - Lexer tokenizer with Item and ItemType definitions
- `promql/parser/generated_parser.y[.go]` - Yacc grammar and compiled parser

**Function & Type System:**
- `promql/parser/functions.go` - Function registry with 80+ PromQL functions
- `promql/parser/value.go` - Value type system (vector, matrix, scalar, string)

**Engine Integration:**
- `promql/engine.go` - Query execution engine
- `promql/functions.go` & `promql/value.go` - Runtime value types and function implementations

**Supporting Components:**
- `promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go` - Error position tracking
- `promql/parser/printer.go`, `prettier.go`, `features.go` - AST output formatting and feature registration

The complete analysis has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with file references, key symbols, execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the parsing pipeline architecture.

\tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), err)\n311: }\n312: \n313: // unexpected creates a parser error complaining about an unexpected lexer item.\n314: // The item that is presented as != \"\" {\n333: \t\terrMsg.WriteString(\", expected \")\n334: \t\terrMsg.WriteString(expected)\n335: \t}\n336: \n337: \tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), errors.New(errMsg.String()))\n338: }\n339: \n340: var errUnexpected = errors.New(\"unexpected error\")\n341: \n342: // recover is the handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of Parse.\n343: func (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\n344: \te := recover()\n345: \tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\n346: \tcase ok:\n347: \t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n348: \t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n349: \t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n350: \n351: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"parser panic: %v\\n%s\", e, buf)\n352: \t\t*errp = errUnexpected\n353: \tcase e != nil:\n354: \t\t*errp = e.(error)\n355: \t}\n356: }\n357: \n358: // Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n359: // It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n360: // Comments are skipped.\n361: //\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n364: // and error handling.\n365: //\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n368: \tvar typ ItemType\n369: \n370: \tif p.injecting {\n371: \t\tp.injecting = false\n372: \t\treturn int(p.inject)\n373: \t}\n374: \t// Skip comments.\n375: \tfor {\n376: \t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n377: \t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n378: \t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n379: \t\t\tbreak\n380: \t\t}\n381: \t}\n382: \n383: \tswitch typ {\n384: \tcase ERROR:\n385: \t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n386: \t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n387: \t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n388: \t\t}\n389: \t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n390: \n391: \t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n392: \t\treturn 0\n393: \tcase EOF:\n394: \t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n395: \t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n396: \tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n397: \t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + posrange.Pos(len(lval.item.Val))\n398: \t}\n399: \n400: \treturn int(typ)\n401: }\n402: \n403: // Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n404: //\n405: // It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\n409: }\n410: \n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\n413: // This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n414: // https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n415: // Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n416: // Trying to inject when a previously injected Item has not yet been consumed will panic.\n417: // Only Item types that are supposed to be used as start symbols are allowed as an argument.\n418: func (p *parser) startSymbolsEnd) {\n424: \t\tpanic(\"cannot inject symbol that isn't start symbol\")\n425: \t}\n426: \n427: \tp.inject = typ\n428: \tp.injecting = true\n429: }\n430: \n431: func (p *parser) provided AST. This includes type checking.\n720: func (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n721: \t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n722: \t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n723: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n724: \tcase Expressions:\n725: \t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n726: \tcase Expr:\n727: \t\ttyp = n.Type()\n728: \tdefault:\n729: \t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n730: \t}\n731: \n732: \t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n733: \t// errors in case of bad typing.\n734: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n735: \tcase *EvalStmt:\n736: \t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n737: \t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n738: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n739: \t\t}\n740: \n741: \tcase Expressions:\n742: \t\tfor _, e := range n {\n743: \t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n744: \t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n745: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n746: \t\t\t}\n747: \t\t}\n748: \tcase \t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n753: \t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n754: \t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n757: \t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n758: \t\t}\n759: \n760: \tcase *BinaryExpr:\n761: \t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n762: \t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n763: \n764: \t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n765: \t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n766: \t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n767: \t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n768: \t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n769: \t\t\t}\n770: \t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n771: \t\t\t}\n772: \t\t\treturn r\n773: \t\t}\n774: \n775: \t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n776: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n777: \t\t}\n778: \n779: \t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n780: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n781: \t\t}\n782: \n783: \t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n784: \t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n785: \t\t}\n786: \n787: \t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n788: \t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n789: \t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n790: \t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n791: If the visitor w returned by\\n346: // v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\\n347: // invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\\n348: // followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\\n349: // As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\\n350: func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\\n351: \\tvar err error\\n352: \\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\\n353: \\t\\treturn err\\n354: \\t}\\n355: \\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\\n356: \\n357: \\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\\n358: \\t\\tif pathToHere == nil {\\n359: \\t\\t\\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\\n360: \\t\\t}\\n361: \\t\\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\\n362: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n363: \\t\\t}\\n364: \\t}\\n365: \\n366: \\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\\n367: \\treturn err\\n368: }\\n369: \\n370: func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\\n371: \\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\\n372: \\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\\n373: \\t\\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\\n374: \\t\\tif ok {\\n375: \\t\\t\\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\\n376: \\t\\t}\\n377: \\t\\treturn nil\\n378: \\t})\\n379: \\treturn selectors\\n380: }\\n381: \\n382: type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\\n383: \\n384: func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\\n385: \\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\\n386: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n387: \\t}\\n388: \\n389: \\treturn f, nil\\n390: }\\n391: \\n392: // Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n393: // f(node, path); node must not be nil. }\\n356: \\n357: // errorf returns an error token and terminates the scan by passing\\n358: // back a nil pointer that will be the next state, terminating l.NextItem.\\n359: func (l *Lexer) Keywords are ignored and\\n672: // scanned as identifiers.\\n673: func lexInsideBraces(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n674: \\tif strings.HasPrefix(l.input[l.pos:], lineComment) {\\n675: \\t\\treturn lexLineComment\\n676: \\t}\\n677: \\n678: \\tswitch r := l.next(); The initial escaping character (\\\\)\\n767: // has already been seen.\\n768: //\\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \\\"go/scanner\\\"\\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n775: \\tvar n int\\n776: \\tvar base, maxVal uint32\\n777: \\n778: \\tch := l.next()\\n779: \\tswitch ch {\\n780: \\tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\\\\\', l.stringOpen:\\n781: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n782: \\tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\\n783: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\\n784: \\tcase 'x':\\n785: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n786: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\\n787: \\tcase 'u':\\n788: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n789: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n790: \\tcase 'U':\\n791: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n792: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n793: \\tcase eof:\\n794: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n795: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n796: \\tdefault:\\n797: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unknown escape sequence %#U\\\", ch)\\n798: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n799: \\t}\\n800: \\n801: \\tvar x uint32\\n802: \\tfor n > 0 {\\n803: \\t\\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\\n804: \\t\\tif d >= base {\\n805: \\t\\t\\tif ch == eof {\\n806: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n807: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n808: \\t\\t\\t}\\n809: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\\\", ch)\\n810: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n811: \\t\\t}\\n812: \\t\\tx = x*base + d\\n813: \\t\\tn--\\n814: \\n815: \\t\\t// Don't seek after last rune.\\n816: \\t\\tif n > 0 {\\n817: \\t\\t\\tch = l.next()\\n818: \\t\\t}\\n819: \\t}\\n820: \\n821: \\tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\\n822: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\\\")\\n823: \\t}\\n824: \\treturn lexString\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\\n828: // represent a valid digit.\\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\\n830: \\tswitch {\\n831: \\tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\\n832: \\t\\treturn int(ch - '0')\\n833: \\tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\\n834: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\\n835: \\tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\\n836: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\\n839: }\\n840: \\n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\\n843: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n844: \\t\\tl.next()\\n845: \\t}\\n846: \\tl.ignore()\\n847: }\\n848: \\n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n871: Loop:\\n872: \\tfor {\\n873: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n874: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n875: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n876: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n877: \\t\\tcase eof:\\n878: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unterminated raw string\\\")\\n879: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n880: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n881: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n882: \\t\\t}\\n883: \\t}\\n884: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n885: \\treturn lexStatements\\n886: }\\n887: \\n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. This case is caught by the parser.\\n987: func (l *Lexer) scanNumber() bool {\\n988: \\tinitialPos := l.pos\\n989: \\t// Modify the digit pattern if the number is hexadecimal.\\n990: \\tdigitPattern \treturn lexStatements\n533: }\n534: \n535: func lexHistogram(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n536: \tswitch l.histogramState {\n537: \tcase histogramStateMul:\n538: \t\tl.histogramState = lexValueSequence\n552: \t}\n553: \n554: \tif l.bracketOpen {\n555: \t\treturn lexBuckets\n556: \t}\n557: \tswitch r := l.next(); {\n558: \tcase isSpace(r):\n559: \t\tl.emit(SPACE)\n560: \t\treturn lexSpace\n561: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n562: \t\tl.backup()\n563: \t\treturn lexHistogramDescriptor\n564: \tcase r == ':':\n565: \t\tl.emit(COLON)\n566: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n567: \tcase r == '-':\n568: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n569: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n570: \tcase r == 'x':\n571: \t\tl.emit(TIMES)\n572: \t\treturn lexNumber\n573: \tcase isDigit(r):\n574: \t\tl.backup()\n575: \t\treturn lexNumber\n576: \tcase r == '[':\n577: \t\tl.bracketOpen = true\n578: \t\tl.gotColon = false\n579: \t\tl.gotDuration = false\n580: \t\tl.emit(LEFT_BRACKET)\n581: \t\treturn lexBuckets\n582: \tcase r == '}' && \t\tcase '+':\n590: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateAdd\n591: \t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n592: \t\tcase '-':\n593: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateSub\n594: \t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n595: \t\tdefault:\n596: \t\t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateNone\n597: \t\t\treturn lexValueSequence\n598: \t\t}\n599: \tdefault:\n600: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"histogram description incomplete unexpected: %q\", r)\n601: \t}\n602: }\n603: \n604: func lexHistogramDescriptor(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n605: Loop:\n606: \tfor {\n607: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); {\n608: \t\tcase isAlpha(r):\n609: \t\t\t// absorb.\n610: \t\tdefault:\n611: \t\t\tl.backup()\n612: \n613: \t\t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n614: \t\t\tif desc, ok := histogramDesc[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n615: \t\t\t\tif l.peek() == ':' {\n616: \t\t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n617: \t\t\t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n618: \t\t\t\t}\n619: \t\t\t\tl.errorf(\"missing `:` for histogram descriptor\")\n620: \t\t\t\tbreak Loop\n621: \t\t\t}\n622: \t\t\t// Current word is Inf or NaN.\n623: \t\t\tif desc, ok := key[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n624: \t\t\t\tif desc == NUMBER {\n625: \t\t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n626: \t\t\t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n627: \t\t\t\t}\n628: \t\t\t}\n629: \t\t\tif desc, ok := counterResetHints[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n630: \t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n631: \t\t\t\treturn lexHistogram\n632: \t\t\t}\n633: \n634: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"bad histogram descriptor found: %q\", word)\n635: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n636: \t\t}\n637: \t}\n638: \treturn lexStatements\n639: }\n640: \n641: func lexBuckets(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n642: \tswitch r := l.next(); {\n643: \tcase isSpace(r):\n644: \t\tl.emit(SPACE)\n645: \t\treturn lexSpace\n646: \tcase r == '-':\n647: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n648: \t\treturn lexNumber\n649: \tcase isDigit(r):\n650: \t\tl.backup()\n651: \t\treturn lexNumber\n652: \tcase r == ']':\n653: \t\tl.bracketOpen = false\n654: \t\tl.emit(RIGHT_BRACKET)\n655: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n656: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n657: \t\t// Current word is Inf or NaN.\n658: \t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n659: \t\tif desc, ok := key[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\n660: \t\t\tif desc == NUMBER {\n661: \t\t\t\tl.emit(desc)\n662: \t\t\t\treturn lexStatements\n663: \t\t\t}\n664: \t\t}\n665: \t\treturn lexBuckets\n666: \tdefault:\n667: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"invalid character in buckets description: %q\", r)\n668: \t}\n669: }\n670: \n671: // lexInsideBraces scans the inside of a vector selector. Keywords are ignored and\n672: // scanned as identifiers.\n673: func lexInsideBraces(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n674: \tif strings.HasPrefix(l.input[l.pos:], lineComment) {\n675: \t\treturn lexLineComment\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tswitch r := l.next(); {\n679: \tcase r == eof:\n680: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"unexpected end of input inside braces\")\n681: \tcase isSpace(r):\n682: \t\treturn lexSpace\n683: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n684: \t\tl.backup()\n685: \t\treturn lexIdentifier\n686: \tcase r == ',':\n687: \t\tl.emit(COMMA)\n688: \tcase r == '\"' || r == '\\'':\n689: \t\tl.stringOpen = r\n690: \t\treturn lexString\n691: \tcase r == '`':\n692: \t\tl.stringOpen = r\n693: \t\treturn lexRawString\n694: \tcase r == '=':\n695: \t\tif l.next() == '~' {\n696: \t\t\tl.emit(EQL_REGEX)\n697: \t\t\tbreak\n698: \t\t}\n699: \t\tl.backup()\n700: \t\tl.emit(EQL)\n701: \tcase r == '!':\n702: \t\tswitch nr := l.next(); {\n732: \tcase r == eof:\n733: \t\treturn lexStatements\n734: \tcase r == '{' && l.peek() == '{':\n735: \t\tif l.histogramState != histogramStateNone {\n736: \t\t\treturn l.errorf(\"unexpected histogram opening {{\")\n737: \t\t}\n738: \t\tl.histogramState = histogramStateOpen\n739: \t\tl.next()\n740: \t\tl.emit(OPEN_HIST)\n741: \t\treturn lexHistogram\n742: \tcase isSpace(r):\n743: \t\tl.emit(SPACE)\n744: \t\tlexSpace(l)\n745: \tcase r == '+':\n746: \t\tl.emit(ADD)\n747: \tcase r == '-':\n748: \t\tl.emit(SUB)\n749: \tcase r == 'x':\n750: \t\tl.emit(TIMES)\n751: \tcase r == '_':\n752: \t\tl.emit(BLANK)\n753: \tcase isDigit(r) || (r == '.' && isDigit(l.peek())):\n754: \t\tl.backup()\n755: \t\tlexNumber(l)\n756: \tcase isAlpha(r):\n757: \t\tl.backup()\n758: \t\t// We might lex invalid Items here but this will be caught by the parser.\n759: \t\treturn lexKeywordOrIdentifier\n760: \tdefault:\n761: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"unexpected character in series sequence: %q\", r)\n762: \t}\n763: \treturn lexValueSequence\n764: }\n765: \n766: // lexEscape scans a string escape sequence. The initial escaping character (\\)\n767: // has already been seen.\n768: //\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \"go/scanner\"\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n775: \tvar n int\n776: \tvar base, maxVal uint32\n777: \n778: \tch := l.next()\n779: \tswitch ch {\n780: \tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\', l.stringOpen:\n781: \t\treturn lexString\n782: \tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\n783: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\n784: \tcase 'x':\n785: \t\tch = l.next()\n786: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\n787: \tcase 'u':\n788: \t\tch = l.next()\n789: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\n790: \tcase 'U':\n791: \t\tch = l.next()\n792: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\n793: \tcase eof:\n794: \t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence not terminated\")\n795: \t\treturn lexString\n796: \tdefault:\n797: \t\tl.errorf(\"unknown escape sequence %#U\", ch)\n798: \t\treturn lexString\n799: \t}\n800: \n801: \tvar x uint32\n802: \tfor n > 0 {\n803: \t\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\n804: \t\tif d >= base {\n805: \t\t\tif ch == eof {\n806: \t\t\t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence not terminated\")\n807: \t\t\t\treturn lexString\n808: \t\t\t}\n809: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\", ch)\n810: \t\t\treturn lexString\n811: \t\t}\n812: \t\tx = x*base + d\n813: \t\tn--\n814: \n815: \t\t// Don't seek after last rune.\n816: \t\tif n > 0 {\n817: \t\t\tch = l.next()\n818: \t\t}\n819: \t}\n820: \n821: \tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\n822: \t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\")\n823: \t}\n824: \treturn lexString\n825: }\n826: \n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\n828: // represent a valid digit.\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\n830: \tswitch {\n831: \tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\n832: \t\treturn int(ch - '0')\n833: \tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\n834: \t\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\n835: \tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\n836: \t\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\n837: \t}\n838: \treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\n839: }\n840: \n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\n843: \tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\n844: \t\tl.next()\n845: \t}\n846: \tl.ignore()\n847: }\n848: \n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n851: Loop:\n852: \tfor {\n853: \t\tswitch l.next() {\n854: \t\tcase '\\\\':\n855: \t\t\treturn lexEscape\n856: \t\tcase utf8.RuneError:\n857: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"invalid UTF-8 rune\")\n858: \t\t\treturn lexString\n859: \t\tcase eof, '\\n':\n860: \t\t\treturn l.errorf(\"unterminated quoted string\")\n861: \t\tcase l.stringOpen:\n862: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n863: \t\t}\n864: \t}\n865: \tl.emit(STRING)\n866: \treturn lexStatements\n867: }\n868: \n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n871: Loop:\n872: \tfor {\n873: \t\tswitch l.next() {\n874: \t\tcase utf8.RuneError:\n875: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"invalid UTF-8 rune\")\n876: \t\t\treturn lexRawString\n877: \t\tcase eof:\n878: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"unterminated raw string\")\n879: \t\t\treturn lexRawString\n880: \t\tcase l.stringOpen:\n881: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n882: \t\t}\n883: \t}\n884: \tl.emit(STRING)\n885: \treturn lexStatements\n886: }\n887: \n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n890: \tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\n891: \t\tl.next()\n892: \t}\n893: \tl.ignore()\n894: \treturn lexStatements\n895: }\n896: \n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. Left comment marker is known to be present.\n898: func lexLineComment(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n899: \tl.pos += posrange.Pos(len(lineComment))\n900: \tfor r := l.next(); !isEndOfLine(r) && r != eof; {\n901: \t\tr = l.next()\n902: \t}\n903: \tl.backup()\n904: \tl.emit(COMMENT)\n905: \treturn lexStatements\n906: }\n907: \n908: // lexNumber scans a number: decimal, hex, oct or float.\n909: func lexNumber(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n910: \tif !l.scanNumber() {\n911: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"bad number syntax: %q\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\n912: \t}\n913: \tl.emit(NUMBER)\n914: \treturn lexStatements\n915: }\n916: \n917: func (l *Lexer) scanDurationKeyword() bool {\n918: \tfor {\n919: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); {\n920: \t\tcase isAlpha(r):\n921: \t\t\t// absorb.\n922: \t\tdefault:\n923: \t\t\tl.backup()\n924: \t\t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n925: \t\t\tkw := strings.ToLower(word)\n926: \t\t\tswitch kw {\n927: \t\t\tcase \"step\":\n928: \t\t\t\tl.emit(STEP)\n929: \t\t\t\treturn true\n930: \t\t\tcase \"range\":\n931: \t\t\t\tl.emit(RANGE)\n932: \t\t\t\treturn true\n933: \t\t\tcase \"min\":\n934: \t\t\t\tl.emit(MIN)\n935: \t\t\t\treturn true\n936: \t\t\tcase \"max\":\n937: \t\t\t\tl.emit(MAX)\n938: \t\t\t\treturn true\n939: \t\t\tdefault:\n940: \t\t\t\treturn false\n941: \t\t\t}\n942: \t\t}\n943: \t}\n944: }\n945: \n946: // lexNumberOrDuration scans a number or a duration Item.\n947: func lexNumberOrDuration(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n948: \tif l.scanNumber() {\n949: \t\tl.emit(NUMBER)\n950: \t\treturn lexStatements\n951: \t}\n952: \t// Next two chars must be a valid unit and a non-alphanumeric.\n953: \tif acceptRemainingDuration(l) {\n954: \t\tl.backup()\n955: \t\tl.emit(DURATION)\n956: \t\treturn lexStatements\n957: \t}\n958: \treturn l.errorf(\"bad number or duration syntax: %q\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\n959: }\n960: \n961: func acceptRemainingDuration(l *Lexer) bool {\n962: \t// Next two char must be a valid duration.\n963: \tif !l.accept(\"smhdwy\") {\n964: \t\treturn false\n965: \t}\n966: \t// Support for ms. Bad units like hs, ys will be caught when we actually\n967: \t// parse the duration.\n968: \tl.accept(\"s\")\n969: \t// Next char can be another number then a unit.\n970: \tfor l.accept(\"0123456789\") {\n971: \t\tfor l.accept(\"0123456789\") {\n972: \t\t}\n973: \t\t// y is no longer in the list as it should always come first in\n974: \t\t// durations.\n975: \t\tif !l.accept(\"smhdw\") {\n976: \t\t\treturn false\n977: \t\t}\n978: \t\t// Support for ms. Bad units like hs, ys will be caught when we actually\n979: \t\t// parse the duration.\n980: \t\tl.accept(\"s\")\n981: \t}\n982: \treturn !isAlphaNumeric(l.next())\n983: }\n984: \n985: // scanNumber scans numbers of different formats. The scanned Item is\n986: // not necessarily a valid number. This case is caught by the parser.\n987: func (l *Lexer) scanNumber() bool {\n988: \tinitialPos := l.pos\n989: \t// Modify the digit pattern if the number is hexadecimal.\n990: \tdigitPattern := \"0123456789\"\n991: \t// Disallow hexadecimal in series descriptions as the syntax is ambiguous.\n992: \tif !l.seriesDesc &&\n993: \t\tl.accept(\"0\") && l.accept(\"xX\") {\n994: \t\tl.accept(\"_\") // eg., 0X_1FFFP-16 == 0.1249847412109375\n995: \t\tdigitPattern = \"0123456789abcdefABCDEF\"\n996: \t}\n997: \tconst (\n998: \t\t// Define dot, exponent, and underscore patterns.\n999: \t\tdotPattern        = \".\"\n1000: \t\texponentPattern   = \"eE\"\n1001: \t\tunderscorePattern = \"_\"\n1002: \t\t// Anti-patterns are rune sets that cannot follow their respective rune.\n1003: \t\tdotAntiPattern        = \"_.\"\n1004: \t\texponentAntiPattern   = \"._eE\" // and EOL.\n1005: \t\tunderscoreAntiPattern = \"._eE\" // and EOL.\n1006: \t)\n1007: \t// All numbers follow the prefix: l.is(digitPattern + dotPattern + underscorePattern + exponentPattern) {\n1014: \t\t// \".\" cannot repeat.\n1015: \t\tif l.is(dotPattern) {\n1016: \t\t\tif dotConsumed {\n1017: \t\t\t\tl.accept(dotPattern)\n1018: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1019: \t\t\t}\n1020: \t\t}\n1021: \t\t// \"eE\" cannot repeat.\n1022: \t\tif l.is(exponentPattern) {\n1023: \t\t\tif exponentConsumed {\n1024: \t\t\t\tl.accept(exponentPattern)\n1025: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1026: \t\t\t}\n1027: \t\t}\n1028: \t\t// Handle dots.\n1029: \t\tif l.accept(dotPattern) {\n1030: \t\t\tdotConsumed = true\n1031: \t\t\tif l.accept(dotAntiPattern) {\n1032: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1033: \t\t\t}\n1034: \t\t\t// Fractional hexadecimal literals are not allowed.\n1035: \t\t\tif len(digitPattern) > 10 /* 0x[\\da-fA-F].[\\d]+p[\\d] */ {\n1036: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1037: \t\t\t}\n1038: \t\t\tcontinue\n1039: \t\t}\n1040: \t\t// Handle exponents.\n1041: \t\tif l.accept(exponentPattern) {\n1042: \t\t\texponentConsumed = true\n1043: \t\t\tl.accept(\"+-\")\n1044: \t\t\tif l.accept(exponentAntiPattern) || l.peek() == eof {\n1045: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1046: \t\t\t}\n1047: \t\t\tcontinue\n1048: \t\t}\n1049: \t\t// Handle underscores.\n1050: \t\tif l.accept(underscorePattern) {\n1051: \t\t\tif l.accept(underscoreAntiPattern) || l.peek() == eof {\n1052: \t\t\t\treturn false\n1053: \t\t\t}\n1054: \n1055: \t\t\tcontinue\n1056: \t\t}\n1057: \t\t// Handle digits at the end since we already consumed before this loop.\n1058: \t\tl.acceptRun(digitPattern)\n1059: \t}\n1060: \t// Empty string is not a valid number.\n1061: \tif l.pos == initialPos {\n1062: \t\treturn false\n1063: \t}\n1064: \t// Next thing must not be alphanumeric unless it's the times token\n1065: \t// for series repetitions.\n1066: \tif r := l.peek(); (l.seriesDesc && r == 'x') || !isAlphaNumeric(r) {\n1067: \t\treturn true\n1068: \t}\n1069: \treturn false\n1070: }\n1071: \n1072: // lexIdentifier scans an alphanumeric identifier. The next character\n1073: // is known to be a letter.\n1074: func lexIdentifier(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n1075: \tfor isAlphaNumeric(l.next()) {\n1076: \t\t// absorb\n1077: \t}\n1078: \tl.backup()\n1079: \tl.emit(IDENTIFIER)\n1080: \treturn lexStatements\n1081: }\n1082: \n1083: // lexKeywordOrIdentifier scans an alphanumeric identifier which may contain\n1084: // a colon rune. If the identifier is a keyword the respective keyword Item\n1085: // is scanned.\n1086: func lexKeywordOrIdentifier(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n1087: Loop:\n1088: \tfor {\n1089: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); {\n1090: \t\tcase isAlphaNumeric(r) || r == ':':\n1091: \t\t\t// absorb.\n1092: \t\tdefault:\n1093: \t\t\tl.backup()\n1094: \t\t\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\n1095: \t\t\tswitch kw, ok := key[strings.ToLower(word)]; {\n1096: \t\t\tcase ok:\n1097: \t\t\t\t// For fill/fill_left/fill_right, only treat as keyword if followed by '('\n1098: \t\t\t\t// This allows using these as metric names (e.g., \"fill + fill\").\n1099: \t\t\t\t// This could be done for other keywords as well, but for the new fill\n1100: \t\t\t\t// modifiers this is especially important so we don't break any existing\n1101: \t\t\t\t// queries.\n1102: \t\t\t\tif kw == FILL || kw == FILL_LEFT || kw == FILL_RIGHT {\n1103: \t\t\t\t\tif !l.peekFollowedByLeftParen() {\n1104: \t\t\t\t\t\tl.emit(IDENTIFIER)\n1105: \t\t\t\t\t\tbreak Loop\n1106: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1107: \t\t\t\t}\n1108: \t\t\t\tl.emit(kw)\n1109: \t\t\tcase !strings.Contains(word, \":\"):\n1110: \\n39: // FunctionCall is the type of a PromQL function implementation\\n40: //\\n41: // vals is a list of the evaluated arguments for the function call.\\n42: //\\n43: // For range vectors it will be a Matrix with one series, instant vectors a\\n44: // Vector, scalars a Vector with one series whose value is the scalar\\n45: // value,and nil for strings.\\n46: //\\n47: // args are the original arguments to the function, where you can access\\n48: // matrixSelectors, vectorSelectors, and StringLiterals.\\n49: //\\n50: // enh.Out is a pre-allocated empty vector that you may use to accumulate\\n51: // output before returning it. The vectors in vals should not be returned.a\\n52: //\\n53: // Range vector functions need only return a vector with the right value,\\n54: // the metric and timestamp are not needed.\\n55: //\\n56: // Instant vector functions need only return a vector with the right values and\\n57: // metrics, the timestamp are not needed.\\n58: //\\n59: // Scalar results should be returned as the value of a sample in a Vector.\\n60: type FunctionCall func(vectorVals []Vector, matrixVals Matrix, args parser.Expressions, enh *EvalNodeHelper) (Vector, annotations.Annotations)\\n61: \\n62: // === time() float64 ===\\n63: func funcTime(_ []Vector, _ Matrix, _ parser.Expressions, enh *EvalNodeHelper) (Vector, annotations.Annotations) {\\n64: \\treturn Vector{Sample{\\n65: \\t\\tF: float64(enh.Ts) / 1000,\\n66: \\t}}, nil\\n67: }\\n68: \\n69: // pickOrInterpolateLeft returns the value at the left boundary of the range.\\n70: // If interpolation is needed (when smoothed is true and the first sample is before the range start),\\n71: // it returns the interpolated value at the left boundary; otherwise, it returns the first sample's value.\\n72: func pickOrInterpolateLeft(floats []FPoint, first int, rangeStart int64, smoothed, isCounter bool) float64 {\\n73: \\tif smoothed && floats[first].T < rangeStart {\\n74: \\t\\treturn interpolate(floats[first], floats[first+1], rangeStart, isCounter)\\n75: \\t}\\n76: \\treturn floats[first].F\\n77: }\\n78: \\n79: // pickOrInterpolateRight returns the value at the right boundary of the range.\\n80: // If interpolation is needed (when smoothed is true and the last sample is after the range end),\\n81: // it returns the interpolated value at the right boundary; otherwise, it returns the last sample's value.\\n82: func pickOrInterpolateRight(floats []FPoint, last int, rangeEnd int64, smoothed, isCounter bool) float64 {\\n83: \\tif smoothed && last > 0 && floats[last].T > rangeEnd {\\n84: \\t\\treturn interpolate(floats[last-1], floats[last], rangeEnd, isCounter)\\n85: \\t}\\n86: \\treturn floats[last].F\\n87: }\\n88: \\n89: // interpolate performs linear interpolation between two points.\\n90: //
